|              සහාපතිතුමාගේ පණවුූඩය

ස්කොට්ලන්ත ජාතික ජින්‌ ලොෝහෝර්‌ ආර්යාව විසින්‌ ලබාදුන්‌ පවුම්‌ 300 මූල්‍ය පරිත්‍යාගයක්‌
මත 1927 මාර්තු 20 දින ආරම්භ කරන ලද ලොෝහෝර්‌ ආර්යා ණය අරමුදල අද වන විට දශක 08 පුරා
එක්‌ අරමුදල පිහිටුවීම සඳහා හේතු පාදක වූ පුද්ගලික අංශයෙන්‌ ණය ලබාගැනීම නිසා රාජා්‍ය හා
පෞද්ගලික අංශයේ සේවකයන්‌ මුහුණ දුන්‌ ණය බරින්‌ පීඩිතවීම අවම කිරීම සඳහා වූ විශිෂ්ට
කාර්යභාරය කට උරදෙමින්‌ සාර්ථක ඉදිරි ගමනක නියැලී ඇත.

අරමුදලක්‌ පිහිටුවීමට අවශ්‍ය මූලික ප්‍රාග්ධනය සඳහා පවුම්‌ 300 ක මුදලක්‌ පරිත්‍යාග කර තිබිණ.
එවකට පුණ්‍ය කොමසාරිස්ව සිටි සී.ර.වී.නැතනියල්ස්‌ පියතුමා අරමුදල පිහිටුවීමේ කාර්යයෙහි
මූලිකව කටයුතු කර ඇති අතර එය 1027 මාර්තු 20 වන දින ලොෝහෝර්‌ ආර්යා ණය අරමුදල
නමින්‌ ආරම්භ කරන ලදී. එමෙන්ම අරමුදල 1051 අංක 38 දරණ ලොෝහෝර්‌ ආර්යා ණය අරමුදල්‌
පනත මගින්‌ ව්‍යවස්ථාපිත ආයතනයක්‌ බවට පනත්‌ විය.

එදා සිට මෙම අරමුදල ප්‍රතිලාභීන්‌ වෙත ණය

චකිය අරමුදලක්‌ ලෙසින්‌ ක්‍රියාත්මක වෙමින්‌ පවති.

3030ක්‌ මෙම අරමුදලේ ප්‍රතිලාභීන්‌ වී ඇත. එම ප්‍රතිලාභීන්‌ පදිංචි දිස්ත්‍ර්‍රක්කය අනුව දෙවන

10.40% ක අඩු වීමක්‌ මෙන්ම ණය මුදල්‌ ප්‍රමාණයේ පෙර වසරට සාපේක්ෂව 3.21% ක අඩු
වීමක්‌ දක්නට ඇත. ප්‍රතිලාභින්ගෙන්‌ 75% අධික පිරිසක්‌ ආරක්ෂක අංශයේ නියුතු පුද්ගලයින්‌

2.2 2018 ණය නිකුත්‌ කිරීමේ ක්‍රියාවලිය හා ප්‍රගතිය

පහත සඳහන්‌ සුදුසුකම්‌ සම්පූර්ණ කළ රාජ්‍ය හො අර්ධ රාජා්‍ය ආයතනවල සේවකයෙකුට මෙම
අරමුදලෙන්‌ ණය අයදුම්‌ කළ හැක.

> විශ්‍රාම වැටුප්‌ සහිත රාජ්‍ය සේවාවේ නියුතු වසර 3 ක අවම ස්ථීර සේවා කාලයක්‌ හිමි
රාජ්‍ය සේවකයකු වීම.

> අර්ධ රාජ්‍ය ආයතනයක සේවකයකු නම්‌ වසර 5 ක අවම ස්ථීර සේවා කාලයක්‌ සපුරා
තිබිම.

> ලබා දෙනු ලබන ණය මුදල්‌ සම්පූර්ණයෙන්ම අයකර ගැනීමට තරම්‌ ප්‍රමාණවත්‌ සේවා
කාලයක්‌ නතිබීම.( විශ්‍රාම ගන්නා වයස්‌ සීමාව අවුරුදු 55 ලෙස සලකයි)

> අයදුම්කරු සඳහා ඉහත සුදුසුකම්‌ සහිත ඇපකරුවන්‌ දෙදෙනෙකු ඉදිරිපත්‌ කිරීම.

> අර්ධ රාජ්‍ය ආයතනයක සේවකයකු නම්‌ ඇපකරුවන්‌ දෙදෙනාගෙන්‌ එක්‌ අයකු අවම
වශයෙන්‌ වසර 03 ක ස්ථීර සේවා කාලයක්‌ පවතින විශ්‍රාම වැටුප්‌ සහිත රාජ්‍ය
සේවාවේ නියුතු අයකු වීම.

> සියළුම ණය අයදුම්කරුවන්ගේ මාසික වේතනයෙන්‌ 40% සීමාව තුල ණය වාරිකය

නිර්දෝශය       පුහුණු ගරු සංචිතය
ආවරණය             රාජ්‍ය භාෂා
කිරීම)           දෙපාර්තමේන්තුවේ
නිර්දෝශිත

නවක නිලධාරීන්‌ සඳහා වන කාර්යාල ක්‍රමවේද හදුන්වා දීමේ මුලික පුභුණුව (Induction
Programme), රාජකාරි විෂයානුබද්ධ දැනුම ලබා දීම මෙන්ම පරිගණක පුහුණුව සඳහා කාර්ය
මණ්ඩළයේ නවක මෙන්ම ස්ථීර සේවකයන්‌ යොමු කිරීම තුලින්‌ ආයතනයේ රාජකාරි කටයුතු
පිළිබදව මනා දැනුමක්‌ ලබා දීම සහ ආයතනයේ රාජකාරීන්‌ පෙරට වඩා කාර්යක්ෂමව හා ඵලදායීව
කර ගෙන යාමත්‌, වෘත්තීය කටයුතු තුල පෙර පැවති තත්ත්වයට වඩා පැහැදිලි ප්‍රගමනයක්‌ දක්නට
ලැබීමත්‌ සුවිශේෂි තත්ත්වයකි.

මෙම පුහුණු වැඩමුළු තුලින්‌ ලබා ගත්‌ දැනුම, කුලසතා භාවිතයෙන්‌ තම රාජකාරි කටයුතු
වියිමත්ව හා ක්‍රමානුකූලවත්‌ කර ගෙන යාමට සේවක මණ්ඩලයට හැකියාව ලැබි ඇත. කාර්ය
මණ්ඩලයේ කාර්යමක්ෂතාවය හා අභිමතාර්ථයන්‌ සාක්ෂාත්‌ කර ගැන්ීමන්‌ පුද්ගල සම්බන්ධතා ඇති
කිරීමට මෙන්ම ලොෝහෝර්‌ ආර්යා ණය අරමුදලේ අරමුණු සාක්ෂාත්‌ කර ගැනීමත්‌ මෙම වාර්ෂික

පුහුණු සැලැස්මට අනුව පුහුණුවීම බෙහෙවින්‌ ඉවහල්‌ විඇත.

සමස්ථ කාර්ය මණ්ඩලයේ පුහුණු ධාරිතාවය ඉහළ නැංවීම සඳහා “කණ්ඩායම්‌ හැගීමෙන්‌
ඔබ්බට” යන දැක්ම පදනම්‌ කරගත්‌ තලගහහේන වතුයාය (Estat), එපිටවල, කිරිඇල්ලහි පිහිටි
“විජය නිවාඩු නිකේතනය” ආයතනය සහ එහි පරිනත මෙන්ම අත්දැකිම්‌ සහිත පුහුණුකරුවන්‌
කණ්ඩායමක්‌ මහින්‌ අභ්‍යන්තරික දෝශන සහ බැහැරගත, ජලාශ්‍රිත මෙන්ම ගොඩබිම්‌ ක්‍රියාකාරකම්‌
වලින්‌ සමන්විත සම්මිශ්‍රණය වූ පුහුණු වැඩසටහනක්‌ වෙත අරමුදලේ සමස්ථ කාර්ය මණ්ඩලය
2018.09.22 වචන දින යොමු කරන ලදී. ඊට අරමුදලේ කාර්ය මණ්ඩලයේ 27 දෙනෙකු ද ඔවුනගේ
පවුල්වල සාමාජිකයින්‌ ඇතුළු සියල්ලන්ම 52 දෙනෙකු මීට සහභාගි වන ලදී.

මෙම බැහැරගත පුහුණු වැඩමුළුව 2017 වසරේ පැවැත්‌ වූ බැහැරගත පුහුණු වැඩමුළුවෙන්‌
වෙනස්‌ වන්නේ මෙය, කාර්ය මණ්ඩලයේ නිලධාරින්‌ සහ ඔවුන්ගේ පවුල්වල සාමාජිකයින්‌ ද සහභාගි
කර ගෙන යෙදුනු එක්‌ දින බැහැරගත පුහුණු වැඩසටහනක්‌ වූ බැවිනි.2018 වසරේ සමස්ථ කාර්ය
මණ්ඩලයම යෙදුනු බැහැරගත පුහුණු වීම තුලින්‌ කාර්ය මණ්ඩල පුහුණුව මෙන්ම ඔවුන්ගේ පවුල්වල
සාමාජිකයන්ගේ ද සහභාගීත්වයෙන්‌ පාරිසරික අත්දැකීම හා විවේකාශ්වාදය ද ලබා ගැනීමට අවස්ථාව

ප්‍රධාන ගිණුම්කරණ පතිපත්ති

1051 අංක 38 දරන ලොෝහොෝර්‌ ආර්යා ණය අරමුදලේ (භාරකාර මණ්ඩලය) පනත
(1956 සංගශෝයිත) මහින්‌ ස්ථාපනය කරන ලද ලොෝහෝර්‌ ආර්යා ණය අරමුදල
ශ්‍රී ලංකාවේ නිත්‍ය්‍යවාසික අරමුදලක්‌. අරමුදලෙහි ලියාපදිංචි කාර්යාලය කොළඹ 02,
සර චිත්තම්පලම්‌ ඒ ගාඩිනර්‌ මාවතෙහි අංක 100,3/2 දරණ ස්ථානයේ පිහිටා ඇත.

අනුකලනතා ප්‍රකාශණය

මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශණ පිළියෙළ කර ඇත්තේ ශ්‍රී ලංකා ගිණුම්කරණ ප්‍රතිපත්තිවලට අනුකූලවය.

2.1

මුල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශණ සඳහා වගකීම

මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශණ සකස්‌ කිරීම සහ ඉදිරිපත්‌ කිරිම සඳහා භාරකාර මණ්ඩලය වගකීම
දරයි.

පිළියෙල කිරීමේ පදනම

ග්‍රී ලංකා රුපියල්‌ වලින්‌ ඉදිරිපත්‌ කර ඇති අරමුදලෙහි මුල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශණ එෙනතිහාසික
පිරිවැය පදනම මත සකස්‌ කර ඇත.

ශේෂපතු දිනට පසු සිදුවිම්‌

සියළුම දාවා්‍ය්‍ය පශ්චාත්‌ ශේෂපත්‍ර සිදුවිම්‌ සැලකිල්ලට ගනු ලැබ ඇති අතර අවශ්‍යතන්හි
මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශන සඳහා වූ අදාල සටහන්‌ වල ගැලපුම්‌ හෝ අනාවරණයන්‌ සිදුකර ඇත.

බදු
වර්තමාන බදු

මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශනයේ සඳහන්‌ වන ආදායම්‌ බදු ගණනය 2018.01.01 දින සිට
2018.03.31 දක්වා කාල පරිච්ඡෙේදයට අදාලව ආදායම්‌ බදු ගණනය කිරිම 20006 අංක
10 දරණ ආදායම්‌ බදු පනතට අනුව ද, 2018.04.01 දන සිට 2018.12.31දක්වාකාල
පරිච්ඡේදය 2017 අංක 24 දරණ සංශෝධිත ආදායම්‌ බදු පනතට අනුව ද ගණනය
කර ඇත.

ආනුශංගික නොරතරු

ණය අරමුදලට අදාල වන ප්‍රතිපත්තීන්‌ වෙනත්‌ ආකාරයකින්‌ විශේෂයෙන්‌ සඳහන්‌
කර ඇත්තනේ නම්‌ මිස, පූර්ව වර්ෂයේ යොදා ගන්නා ලද ප්‍රතිපත්තීන්‌ හා අනුකුල වේ.
ප්‍රවර්ථන වර්ෂයේ ඉදිරිපත්‌ කිරීම තහවුරු කිරීම පිණස අවශ්‍ය අවස්ථාවන්හි ද පූර්ව
වර්ෂයේ සංඛ්‍යා නැවත පිළියෙල කර තිබේ.

වත්කම්‌ සහ එහි වටිනාකම්‌ තක්සේරු කිරීමේ පදනම

බොල්‌ ණය සහ අඩමාන ණය සදහා ප්‍රතිපාදන

බොල්‌ ණය සහ අඩමාන ණය සඳහා ප්‍රතිපාදන සපයනු ලබන්නේ භාරකරුවන්‌
විසින්‌ සිදුකරනු ලබන සමාලෝචන පදනම්‌ කරගෙන වන අතර පාරිභොෝගිකයින්‌
සදහා වූ ණය වාර්තාකරනු ලබන කාල සීමාව අවසානයේදි ඉදිරියට ගෙන යන ලද

ද දක්වා තිබේ.මෙම වත්කම්‌ පහත සඳහන්‌ කර ඇති සමුච්චිත ක්ෂය කිරිම්‌ අඩුකර
ලැබෙන පිරිවැයට දක්වා ඇත.

පිණිසය.

විශ්‍රාම වැටුප්‌ හා විශ්‍රාම ප්‍රතිලාභ 1983 අංක 12 දරණ පාරිතෝෂික ගෙවිම්‌ පනත

04.        ආදායම්‌ ප්‍රකාශනය

4.1 ආදායම්‌ හඳුනා ගැනීම

4.1.1 ණය පොලී ආදායම
ණය පොලී ආදායම උපචිත පදනම මත ගණනය කර ඇත.
රාජ්‍ය අංශයේ සේවකයන්ට ලබාදුන්‌ ණය වලින්‌ මාස 03 ක්‌ සඳහා ණය ප්‍රතිපාදන
නොලැබුණු කියාකාරී නොවන ණය පිළිබද අරමුදල අවධානය යොමු කරන අතර
ඉන්‌ පසුව එම ණය මත ලැබෙන පොළිය මුදල්‌ පදනම මත ගණනය කරනු ලබයි.

4.1.2 බ      0ංදායම
බදු ගිවිසුම මත අරමුදල්‌ පරිශ්‍රයේ පදිංචිට සිටින කුලී නිවැසියන්ගේ ගොඩනැගිලි
කුලී ආදායම උපචිත පදනම මත හදුනාගෙන ඇත.

4.1.3 වියදම්‌ හඳුනාගැනීම

ණය අරමුදල අඛන්ඩව පවත්වාගෙන යාමට සහ ස්ථාවර වත්කම්‌ කාර්යක්ෂමව
පවත්වාගෙන යාමෙහිලා ජනිත වන සියළුම වියදම්‌ වසරේ ලාහය ගණනයේදී
ආදායමෙන්‌ අඩුකර පෙන්වයි.

යම්‌ වත්කමක පවත්නා ස්වභාවය වැඩිදියුණු කිරීමට ව්‍යාප්ත කිරීමට වත්කමක්‌
අත්පත්‌ කර ගැන්ම වෙනුවෙන්‌ දරනු ලබන හෝ ණය අරමුදලෙහි ඉපයීම්‌ ධාරිතාව
වැඩිදියුණු කිරීමෙහිලා ජනිත වන සියළුම වියදම්‌ ප්‍රාග්ධන වියදම්‌ ලෙස සලකනු
ලබයි.

ලෝහෝර්‌ ආර්යා ණය අරමුදල

2018 දෙසැම්බර්‌ 31 දිනට මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශනයන්ට අදාළ සටහන්‌

17      අනෙකුන්‌ වගක්ම්‌

ගොඩනැගිලි කුලි තැම්පතු
උපචිත වියදම්‌

රාජ්‍ය සේවකයන්‌ සඳහා ලබාදුන්‌ ණය මුදල්‌

වැඩිපූර අයකර ගැනීම

ණය ගිමියන්‌
අනෙකුත්‌ තැම්පතු - ආරක්ෂක

17.1 ගොඩනැගිලි කුලි තැම්පත්‌
ජාතික ඉතිරි කිරීමේ බැංකුව
ලංකා විදුලිබල මණ්ඩලය
ලංකා විදුලිබල මණ්ඩලය - තොරතුරු
තාක්ෂණ අංශය
සමුපකාර සේවක කොමිෂන්‌ සහාව
ඒ. ජේ.එස්‌.ඇසෝසියේටඩ්‌ ආයතනය

රාජ්‍ය ව්‍යවසාය ප්‍රතිසංස්කරණ කොමිෂන්‌

සහාව

17.2 ගෙවිය යුතු වියදම්‌
නඩත්තු - ගොඩනැගිලි
මුද්‍රණ හා ලිපිද්‍රව්‍ය

ආරක්ෂක ගාස්තු

විදුලිය

ගොඩැනැගිලි

විගණන ගාස්තු

එකතු කළ අගය මත බදු
දුරකථන

ජාතිය ගොඩැනැගීමේ බද
මුද්දර ගාස්තු

ජලය

පාලන භාරකාරතුමාගේ දීමනා
වාර්ෂික ප්‍රසාද දීමනා
විශේෂ දීමනා

වෘත්තීය ගාස්තු

183      බදුකරණය සඳහා ප්‍රතිපාදන
වසර ආරම්භයේ දී ශේෂය
වසර සඳහා වූ ප්‍රතිපාදන
බදු ගෙවීම්‌
රඳවා ගැනීමේ බද
පෙර වසර සඳහා ප්‍රතිපාදන
වසර අවසාන ශේෂය

19 මූදල්‌ අමංාත්‍ය්‍යාංශයීය ලැබීම්‌
වසර ආරම්භයේ ශේෂය
වසර තුල පරිවර්තන
වසර අවසාන ශේෂය

වසර ආරම්භයේ ශේෂය
වසර සඳහා වූ ප්‍රතිපාදන
වසර තුල දී ගෙවීම්‌

Lady Lochore Loan Fund

Vision
To be a leading financial supporter for the employees of
Government, Public co-operations, Statutory institutions and
Members of the three Forces.

Mission
To contribute in creating a contented Public Service by
releasing Employees of Government, Public co-operations,
Statutory institutions and Members of the three Forces from
indebtedness.

Objective
To relieve Indebtedness of Employees of the Government,
Public co-operations, statutory institutions and Members of the
three Force, by providing short term loans without delay on
concessionary interest rates under casy terms.

Functions
> Providing Loans to clients by maintaining the Fund
sustainably.
> Improving institutional promotion and Comparative
capacity.

Formulation and implementation of procedures for raising
funds and maintaining the Fund.
Developing best practices for loan management, efficiently
lending and improving lending facilities.
Acting as an casy facilitator of implementation of Loan
Schemes for the Employees of the other Government
Institutions.
Dealing with a proper financial control system in Lending
and maintaining Loan affairs.

Establishment:

> Lady Lochore Loan Fund has been established under the Act No. 38 of
1051 (amended in 1053) and it is being operated under the purview of the

Ministry of Finance.

           PRESIDENT'S M ESSAGE

Lady Lochore Loan Fund was established on 26 March 1027 on a
financial donation of £300 from a Scottish national, Lady Jean Lochore. As of today
for cight decades the Fund has shouldered an excellent role of minimizing the
burden of debt faced by employees of public and private sector who have been
burrowing from the private sector which is the reason that the Fund was established
and has engaged on a successful journey forward.

Especially, Today the community has faced a major transformation in the
economic, political, religious, ethnic and educational Sphere than in 1027.
Accordingly, long term, medium term and Short term debt schemes have been
introduced to meet the diverse loan requirements of public and private Sector
employees while providing successful solutions for these transformative courses. In
consideration of the types of loans in the existing commercial banking system, these
loan Schemes introduced are more conducive and flexible in terms of credit
conditions, collateral requirements, loan interest rates and recovery period. AS a
result, the number of applicants seeking for loans has increased steadily.

During my tenure of office for the last three years, a Special programme
had been launched to transform the functions of the Fund beyond the traditional role
of the Lady Lochore Loan Fund.

Especially, the matters Such as operating activities of the Fund in
accordance with existing rules and regulations, utilizing the latest technology in the
operation of functions of the Fund whenever possible, designing the operations of
the organization to suit future economic developments, providing necessary
facilities and incentives for the employees to accomplish more friendly and cfficient
Service, introducing and maintaining an appropriate Accounting system to suit with
more transparent accountability method of resource utilization of the Fund, and
applying Public Sector Accounting Standards for the preparation of accounts to
Subject the functions of the Fund to the Auditor General's direct audit are included
with the Same.

In comparison with the previous year, significant progress had been made in
financial performance of the Fund. The surplus of pre-tax profit has increased by
11% over the previous year and the Fund had to pay 26.7% of heavy tax in the year
2018 compared to the year 2017 due to non-receipt of tax relicf as in previous
years. AS a result, the surplus after the tax deduction is reduced by 7%.

Considering the financial position in the year 2018, the financial stability of
the Fund has increased and especially the net asset value has approximately
increased by 0% especially compared to the year 2017. Accordingly, the stability of
the Fund has been steadily improved in every year and especially, it is a great
achievement that the Fund has been able to operate within and build Such a strong
financial position without receiving any funds from the Ministry of Finance, and it
would be a great example for other Institutions that rely on Government Funds.


Also, the contributions of all the cmployees including the Board of Trustees
to the progress of the Fund should be commended. It is very difficult for the
financial institutions engaged with Such matters to show a Continuous progress
especially on annual basis. The financial losses incurred by the Fund especially due
to default in debt repayment arc immense. However, due to the recovery
methodology followed by the Fund, such loan repayment defaults could be Kept to
a minimum level.

The Fund has developed and employee incentive scheme to enhance
employee motivation based on their performance, and it is an additional
qualification for the cfficient employees to receive higher incentive on their
Commitment and on their promotions.

Accordingly, I assure that I will act with the full cooperation of the staff to
further develop its pertormance Shown during the year 2018 with the objective of
making the Fund as the foremost public Sector lending institution in the Future.

MESSAGE OF M ANAGING TRUSTEE

Lady Lochore Loan Fund (LLLE) was
founded on February 17™ February, 1027
by Lady Jean Lochore, who later became
a citizen of Sri Lanka (Ceylon), and wife
of a Millionaire Businessman from
Scotland, UK, with the help of Rev. Fr.
C.E.v. Nathanielz of Colombo and
established under the Lady Lochore Loan
Fund Act No.3$8 of 1051 under the
Ministry of Finance. Since then it has
been managed by the Managing Trustee
under the Supervision and direction of a
Board of Trustees appointed by the
Minister of Finance.l took over office of
the LLLF as the Managing Trustee (Head of the Organization) on 27" February, 2015
with the formation of the Yahapalana Government on the 08:7 anuary, 2015 under HE
President, Maithripala Sirisena and Hon. Prime Minister, Ranil Wickremesinghe.
Being the retired Senior Public Servant of the Sri Lanka Administrative Service (SLAS)
and having held high executive positions in the Public Service, my first move was to
Study the organization and its operations well and have been able to set my foot on re-
Structuring the cntity to what it is today with the express approval of the Board of
Trustees. Within two years of my assuming duties as the Managing Trustee the
processes of granting loans to public Servants had been simplified and the
administration, accounting and IT sectors of the LLLFE streamlined to meet the
challenges and the nceds of the day in the competitive markets faced by the lending
institutions where the socio-economic needs and advanced technology have been rapidly
Srowing.

The maximum amount of loan of Rs. 50,000/-provided for nearly 30 years has been
raised to higher amounts and today the Public Servants who are in financial distress can
enjoy our loan scheme that grants Rs. 100,000/- to non-staff Public Servants, RS.
175,000/- to non-stafft Public Servants who stagnate in their initial grades for longer
period of time due to various reasons, and Rs.250,000/-and Rs.300,000/-to staff-grade
officers in the Public Service.

According to the simplified mechanism in place as at date, the loan application is
processed and released within one week as against nearly two to three months to get the
Ioan passed in the past. A loan applicant has to visit the LLLEF only two occasions as
against five times in the past and the loan application can be downloaded from the LLLF
Website in all three languages from any part of the island nation. We arc able to carry
out this enormous task due to the cfficiently functioning Board of Trustees and the
magnificent team work of the staff under my able guidance and leadership without any
Srant from the Ministry or budgetary allocation from the Government.

However, the LLLE has now begun to face problems in issuing loans within three days
due to lack of funds resulting from big amounts being disbursed as loans and the
demand for loans has increased in multiple proportions. To overcome this crisis, we
have now started regulating the issue of loans in such a manner that no loan applicant is
refused of granting loans but the time period involved in processing the loan


applications and issuance of cheques is limited to one month duration. It is crystal clear
that the LLLF needs financial assistance from the Ministry to continue to provide a
better Service to the majority of the Public Servants and if the Ministry accommodates
the request made by the Board of Trustees to grant the LLLF at least Rs.50O0Mn as an
interest-free loan to establish ten (10) Branch Offices of the LLLF in 10 Selected
District Secretariats to extend our Services to those public Servants who could reach
those ten Branch Offices with no hassle and inconvenience and obtain loans. The Hon.
Mangala Samaraweera, Minister of Finance having studied our request and understood
the plight of the Public Servants, who appreciate and admire the services rendered by the
LLLE and the importance of its existence, agreed to grant us a loan of RS.50OMn
through the Budget Proposal of 2020. The 1.4Mn Public Servants of this country will
no doubt be grateful to him and the Government of Sri Lanka.

On the whole, the economic efficiency of the Organization and the productivity level of
the work force have been remarkably enhanced through the staff training scheme put in
place according to its training needs, and the welfare of the work force is given pride of
place to enable them to achieve Self-satisfaction and sclf-actualization in the work place.
A vibrant Performance Appraisal Scheme has been introduced to decide on the payment
of Annual Bonus to the staff of the LLLF and this scheme has enormously induced the
trend of motivation and cmpowerment among the staff as a whole.

The building of LLLEF which was not repaired for the last 50 years and was in a
dilapidated condition has been fully refurbished with all modern facilitics and also
action has already been taken to beautify the office and the reception areas to enable the
workforce and the clients who patronize the LLLF to do their business transactions in a
very conducive, pleasant and healthy atmosphere.

The number of loans granted was around 3700 in the year 201§,as against around 4100
in the year 2017, and the quantum of loan released per month was around Rs.30Mn the
year 2018 as against Rs.3IMn in the year 2017.The decline in both the issuance of
loans and quantum of loans granted in the year 2018 was due to the decline in the
demand for loans. However, a new loan scheme was planned to introduce in 2010
in order to overcome this situation. Also, the monthly rental received from five tenants
who occupy the 2™ and 1: Floors of LLLF is around Rs.2 Mn, with which the LLLF
meets 3/4 of its monthly recurrent and operational expenditure and the profits
gencrated from granting of loans are added to the profit of the LLLFE. The annual profit
carned by the LLLEF after taxation stands at around 41IMn in the year 2017 as against
around RS.33Mn the year 2018. In fact, we made a strong request to the Hon.
Minister of Finance to direct the Inland Revenue Department to exempt taxing the
income derived from the interest on loans granted to Public Servants so that we
would be able to utilize the cxempted amount from taxation to grant more loans to
the deserving public servants. We do agree that the taxation is part and parcel of the
Government revenue carning process but a Service oriented Organization like LLLF
that serves only the public servants who are in financial distress without any grant or
budgetary allocation from the Government, solely depending on its income on the
interest on loans issued, Should be cxempted from Taxation. The LLLEF was
exempted from Income Tax but with the introduction of the new Income Tax Act of
Inland Revenuc Act No 24 of 2017 dated of the Inland Revenue Department, this
privilege was done away with. However, we have made a strong appeal to the Ministry
of Finance to consider exempting the LLLEF from income tax through the next Budget.


A Complaint Box is placed for the benefit of the clients who have any
complaint/suggestion to be brought to the notice of the Management and all such
complaints/sugsestions are attentively looked into daily and attended to by the
Managing Trustee along with the relevant officials concerned. We found that most of
the complaints made by the customers are focused on undue delays in refunding the
monies in the form of additional installment payments that have come into LLLF
Account. We have been able to rectify this situation by crediting the excess amounts of
money received in the Account of the LLLE, direct to the client's Account enabling
them not to visit the LLLF for the refund.

The objectives of the LLLEF for which it was founded by Lady Jean Lochore have now
been achieved, and all Public Servants in the 25 Districts of Sri Lanka have been able
to enjoy equally and with no discrimination or delay, the loan facilities provided by the
LLLF.

Iwould like to make use of this opportunity to extend my sincere gratitude to the Hon.
Minister, State Minister and Secretary of the Ministry of Finance and others who gave
us the guidance and support, and also to the Board of Trustees, officials of the Fund who
stood by me always and made their contributions to makc my endeavors Successful in
managing the LLLE. I would continue to go forward with my creative, innovative and
competitive ideas and efforts to strengthen the LLLF for the betterment of the Public
Servants who have developed great hopes and reliance on LLLF and its ycomen Services
extended to them.

S. Winston Pathiraja
Managing Trustee,
Lady Lochore Loan Fund.




01
BACKGROUND OF THE FUND

| EK ~

An initial capital of 300 Sterling pounds for the establishment of the Loan Fund
had been donated by Lady Jean Lochore, who was a Scott national and lived in Sri Lanka
for a long period. Then the Commissioner of Charity, Reverend Father C.E.V.Nathanielz
had taken initiatives to establish the Fund on 26" March 1027 and it was named as Lady
Lochore Loan Fund. The Fund was transformed into a Statutory Body by the Lady
Lochore Loan Fund Act No. 38 of 1051.

Since then by granting loans and
recovering loans, the Fund has functioning as a
revolving fund, as the existing banking system
was not Supportive of fulfilling short-term
financial requirements of the employees of the
public and Private Sector Institutions, they were
compelled to obtain loans at very high interest
rates from outside lending organizations or from
individuals. Due to this reason, the employees
of the public sector as well as private sector
were Suffering from indebtedness immensely.
The establishment of the Lady Lochore Loan
Fund had brought a great relict to all these
employees concerned. After the establishment
of this Fund as a Statutory Body in 1051, a three
storied building owned by this institution was
constructed with the donations received from
the government and other donors.

Lady Jean Lochore
1.1 Board of Trustees

Board of Trustees consists of qualified
representatives from the public and private
Sectors appointed by Hon. Minister of
Finance. The patron of this institution is
held by the Minister of Finance. The
Managing Trustee for administration
purposes of the Fund is appointed from the
members appointed to the Board of
Trustees, as per the section 10 and 11 of the
Act of the Lady Lochore Loan Fund. AS
per the clause 5 of the said Act, the post of
the President of the Fund is held by the
Treasury Representative.

2.2 Loan Procedure and the Progress 20183

Employees in Government or Semi government Sector, who have the following
qualifications, could apply for loans from this Fund.

>

Be a pensionable public officer who has completed minimum of 03 years
permanent service in government sector.

A semi-government employee should complete minimum of 05 years of
permanent Service.

Should have sufficient service period for recovering the loan amount prior to
the retirement. (The age is considered as 55 years)

Two guarantors for the applicant with qualifications maintained above.

For an employee of a semi government sector, one of the two guarantors
Should be a public officer who has completed minimum of 03 years of
permanent Service in government Sector.

Ability to recover the loaned amount within the 40% limit of loan applicant's
monthly Salary.

The progress of processing the loan applications submitted by the qualified loan
applicants as mentioned above and issuing of loans in the year 2018 are the follows:

2.3 Issued Loan Categories and Monitory Values of Loans

Through initializing a new loan category of Rs.300,000/- to generate a higher income on
interest from the year 2018 and amending the maximum loan limit granted for an
average government Servant up to Rs.250,000/- from the year 2018, the demand for
above loan and Categories has been Consequently by 4000% and 77%. On this
incensement, a higher portion of the loan Capital were directed towards these loan
Categories thus it has limited the loan capital resulting in limitation of loan issued. This
Limitation has comparatively decreased the number of loans 10.40% from previous year
and amount of loan compared to previous year decreased by 3.22%. Compared to

previous year, income on loan interest has achieved a positive grant by 0.05%.

2.5.2 Sustainability of the Fund

Special attention of the board of trustees had drawn on maintaining the
operational and the financial sustainability of the Fund. As this institution is not
depending on the rants of the Treasury or budgetary provisions, all the expenses
including salaries of the cadre and other operational costs are met by the interest income
of the Fund and the rental of the building. Covering all the operational expenses Such as
bad debts, administrative and other expenses for recovery of loans, the surplus had
invested at National Savings Bank and People’s Bank ensuring the sustainability of the

Fund.

2.5.3 Operational Income

During the year 2018 the total Operational Income was Rs.102 million while the net
operational Surplus was RS.33.1 million. Operational Income and the net operational
Surplus of the year 2017 were O07 and 41.6 million respectively. As a result of growth in
the interest income on fixed deposits, increasement of other incomes and the amount
indicated after made the payment and transferring of two Motor vehicles received from
the Ministry of Finance as donations of the Finance Ministry in the final accounts
which should be accrued to the profit from the years 2016 to 2020 thus from the total
value the portion which belongs to the year 20106 and 2017 when added to the annual
income, caused a growth in operational income in the year 2018 by 4.71% when
compared to year 2017. However, the interest carned on any loan granted by Lady
Lochore Loan Fund under the Inland Revenuc Amendment Act No 19 of 2000 is
exempt from income tax as defined in Section 132 of the Inland Revenue Act No 10 of
2006. As a result, by the end of the first quarter of the year 2018, huge expenditure born
on income tax Caused approximately 0.00% decrease in net operational Surplus in
parallel with the increase in income of the year 2013.

plan had immensely helped in achieving efficiency and objectives of the staff establishing
personal relationships as well as achieving the objectives of the Lady Lochore Loan Fund.

On 22. 00. 2018 the staff of the Fund was directed to undergo a mixed training
programme consisting of internal lectures, outdoor, water and ground activities under a
guidance of matured and an experienced group of trainers of ““Wijaya Holiday Resort” at
Thalagahahena Estate in Epitawala, Kiriclla an institute based on the vision “Beyond
The Team Feeling”. In order to increase the training capacity of the entire staff. 27
members of the staff of the Fund and family members of them
had participated in this training event.

This out bound training programme which had been participated by the officers of
the Fund and their family members was different from the outbound training workshop held
in the year 2017. Outbound training held in the year 2018 which was participated by the
entire Staff and their family members gave a special opportunity of gaining staff training,
environmental experience as well as enjoyment of relaxation to all.

Modernization and Renovation in the Premises of the Fund

The Lady Lochore Loan Fund building, built inlool, had not been
renovated for several decades, thus the renovation and modernization of the
Fund building complex to Suit the present was initiated in November 2015. The
Civil Security Department, Selected by a systematic procedure on approval of
the 828" Meeting of the Board of Trustees was renovated the building
completely. The consultancy service of Same had been assigned to the State
Development and Construction Corporation (SDE&CC) and the project was
successfully completed the renovation of the basement of the Fund building and
the official residence in the year 2013.

Accordingly, most of the renovation work of the Fund building has becn
completed by the end of 2018, by paying an amount of Rs.4, 532,134.11 of the
total estimated cost of Rs. 23, 462,043.60. Essential renovation of the basement
of the Fund building and the official residence have been completed by only
paying a sum of Rs. 305,430.01 in the year 2013.

Regularization of Staff Administration and Office Systems

Training of the Staff according to an annual training plan approved —
Enhance the ability of the organization to provide continuous and uninterrupted,
cfticient and quality service to its clients through training new and permanent
Staff on an annual training plan approved by the Board of Trustees.

Introducing a new complex performance appraisal system —Staff
Performance Evaluation of the entire staff had been initiated in a more
transparent and optimum manner with a morc rational and practical
methodology, completely reversing the existing employee performance
appraisal System while planning to pay the Annual Bonus based on monthly
salary according to the percentage score earned by the staff for their
performance appraisal.

Introduction of Bar Examination and Language Proficiency Examination
for the Promotion of Staff — Establishment of the fundamental basis for
obtaining the highest quality of service by Introducing to the staff the
Efficiency Bar Examination which was not available in the Fund so far. For this
purpose, the staff was directed to sit for the Efficiency Bar Examination
conducted by the Department of Technical Education and Training.
Organizing a training programme to provide Tamil Language Knowledge to the
Staff who required to sit successfully for the Tamil Language Proficiency
Examination and direct the staff to the same examination conducted by the
Department of Technical Education and Training.

By conducting regular staff meetings of the Heads of the Department on a
monthly basis and by conducting meetings for the entire staff on tri-monthly
basis, resolved the grievances of the staff after formal cxamination, reviewed
and established new proposals and fulfilled improvement of the staff.

Stat Loan

A new change in the staff loan scheme of the Fund and expanding the Limits of
the Rs. 250.000 loan available to the staff at 11.5% interest rate was relaxed in
2018 under the approval of the 866" meeting of the Board of Trustees.

Accordingly, in respect of the collateral issues which the staff of the Fund may
face in obtaining loans, Fund has allowed officers of external government
institutions to submit as their guarantors for the loan, subject to all conditions in
the same manner as the Fund grants loans to officers of external government
institutions.

Land deeds and Bonds

At the time of initiations of the Fund; granting of Loans on the surety of

deeds of land was conducted. Since 1060, the Fund is responsible for 267 surety bonds
taken in under this method. As this method of granting Loans is no longer in operation,
the Audit Committee has recommended to relcase the surety bonds according to the
relevant office of District Land Registrar and complete the release by registering the
cancellation of surety under the names mentioned in the bonds. Meeting of §31' Board
of Trustees has approved the release the said bonds accordingly. Thus 101 bonds had
been released as at 31.12.2013.

To the members of Lady Lochore Loan Fund

CHARTERED AUUOUNTANTN
BUMITIL RANWATTA satis twa Yes Pair Pind

Report on the Audit of the Financial Statements

Opinion

We have audited the financial statements of Lady Lochore Loan Fund, which comprise the Statement
of financial position as at December 31, 2018 and the statement of comprehensive income, Statement
of changes in equity and Statement of each cash flows for the year then ended and notes to the
financial Statements including a summary of significant accounting policies.

Im our opinion the accompanying financial statements give a true and fare view of the financial
position of the Fund as at December 31, 2018 and of its financial performance and its cash flows for
the year then ended in accordance with Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standards (SLPSAS).

Basis for opinion

We conducted our audit in accordance with the Sri Lanka Auditing Standards (SLAuSS). Our
responsibilities under those standards are further described in the Auditor's Responsibilities for the
Audit of the Financial Statements section of our report. We are independent of the Fund in accordance
with the ethical requirements of the Code of Ethics issued by CA Sri Lanka (Code of Ethics) that are
relevant to our audit of the financial Statements, and we have fulfilled our other ethical responsibilities
in accordance with the Code of Ethics. We believe that the audit evidence we have obtained is
Sufficient and appropriate to provide a basis for our opinion.

Responsibilities of Management and those Charged with Governance for the Financial
Statements.

Management is responsible for the preparation of financial statements that give a true and fare view in
accordance with Sri Lanka Accounting Standards and for such internal control as management
determines is necessary to enable the preparation of financial statements that are free from material
misstatements, whether due to fraud or error.

In preparing the financial Statements, management is responsible for assessing the Fund’s ability to
Continue as a going concern, disclosing, as applicable, matters related to going concern and using the
going concern basis of accounting unless management cither intends to liquidate the Fund or to cease
operations, or has no realistic alternative but to do So.

Those charged with governance are responsible for overseeing the Fund’ s financial reporting process.

Auditor’s Responsibilities for the Audit of the Financial Statements.

Our objectives are to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements as a whole
are free from material misstatement whether due to fraud error and to issue an auditor's report that
includes our opinion. Reasonable assurance is a high level of assurance but is not a guarantee that an
audit conducted in accordance with SLAuSS will always detect a material misstatement when it exists.
Misstatements Can arise from fraud or error and are considered material if, individually or in the
aggregate, they could reasonably be expected to influence the economic decisions of users taken on the
basis of these financial statements.

A further description of the auditor’s responsibilities for the audit of the financial statements is located
at Sri Lanka Accounting (and Auditing Standards Committee website at:
http://slaasc .com/auditing/auditorsresponsibilty.php. This description forms part of our auditor’s
report.

Report on Other Legal and Regulatory Requirements
None

LADY LOCHORELOAN FUND
NOTES TO THE FINANCIAL STATEMENTS FOR THE YEAR ENDED
DECEMBER 31, 2018

1.        Principal Accounting Policies

General Information

The Lady Lochore Loan Fund is established by Lady Lochore Loan
Fund(Board of Trustees) Act No 38 of 1o51(Revised 1050) and the fund is

domiciled in Sri Lanka.The registered office of the Fund is located at 100-
3/2, Sir Chittampalam A Gardiner Mawatha,Colombo 02.

1.1 Statement of Compliance

The Financial Statements have been prepared in accordance with Sri
Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standards (SLAS).

1.2 Responsibility of Financial Statements

The board of Trustees is responsible for the preparation and
presentation of the Financial Statements.

1.3 Basis of Preparation

The Financial Statement of the Fund presented in Sri Lanka Rupees,
have been prepared on a historical cost basis.

1.4 Events occurring after the Balance Sheet Date

All material post Balance Sheet events have been considered and where
appropriate adjustments to or disclosures have been made in the
respective Notes to the Financial Statements.

1.5 Taxes

Current tax

The provision for income tax is based on the elements of the income
and expenditure as reported in the financial statements and computed in
accordance with the provisions of the Inland Revenue Act No 10 of
2006 and amendments thereto for the period from 01.01.2018 to
31.03.2018 and Inland Revenue Act No. 24 of 2017 for the period from
01.04.2018 to 31.12.2018.

Comparative Information

The accounting policies applied by the Loan Fund are unless otherwise
Stated, consistent with those used in the previous year. Previous year’s
figures and phrases have been re-arranges, where necessary, to confirm
to the current year’s presentation.

31


02. ASSETS AND BASES OF THEIR VALUATION

2.1 Provision for Loan Losses
Provision for Bad and Doubtful Loans are made on the basis of a review
made by the Trustee s loans from customers are stated at the outstanding

Carried forward balances less provision made as at the end of the Reporting
period.

2.2 Fixed deposits

Fixed deposits and other interest bearing Securities held for resale in the
near future to benefit from short term market movement are accounted for
at cost plus the relevant proportion of the discount or premium.

2.3 Property. Plant &Equipment

Property Plant & Equipment is stated at cost of purchase together with any
incidental expenses thereon. The assets are stated at cost less accumulated
depreciation, which is provided for on the basis specified below.

Building                                                   4%
Computer Equipment                                  25%
Furniture and Fittings                                10%
Office Equipment                                      10%
Electrical Fixtures and Fittings                    10%
Motor Vehicle                                              25%

From the year 2008/00, the Loan Fund has changed its accounting policy to
provide depreciation from the month of purchase to the month of disposal.
Up to the year 2007/08, depreciation was not provided on the assets

purchased and used during the year also no depreciation was provided in
the year of disposal.

2.4 Other Receivables

Other receivables are stated at the amounts they are estimated to realize.

2.5 Cash & Cash Equivalents

Cash and Cash Equivalents are defined as cash in hand and demand deposit
and short term liquid investment readily convertible to identified amounts
of cash and subject to insignificant risks of changes in value. The cash
Flow Statement has been prepared using the indirect Method.

32


03. LIABILITIES AND PROVISIONS

All known liabilities have been provided in preparing the financial
Statements.

3.1 Capital Commitments

Capital commitments of the Loan Fund are disclosed in the respective notes
to the Financial Statements.

3.2 Pensions and Retirement Benefits

A provision has been made for Retiring Gratuity Payable under the
payment of Gratuity Act No.l2 of 1083.This Provision has been computed
in accordance with the gratuity formula adopted by the board of Trustees.

3.3 Defined Contribution Plans-Emplovees’ Provident Fund and Emplovees
“Trust Fund

All employee are cligible for Lady Lochore staff provident Fund
contributions and Employee's Trust Fund contributions in linc with
respective Statues and regulations. The loan Fund contributes 16% of gross
emoluments or employees to Lady Lochore staff provident Fund and 3%
of gross emoluments of ecmployees to the Employees ‘Trust Fund which
are externally funded.

04. INCOME STATEMENT

4.1 Revenue Recognition

4.1.1 Imterest Income

Interest Income recognized on an accrual basis. The Fund considers Loans
granted to Government employees from whom recoveries have ceased for
3 months as “Non Performing Loans’. Thereafter the interest is recognized
on Such loans on cash basis.

4.1.2 Rental Income

Rent income is recognized on an accrual basis.

4.1.3 Expenditure Recognition

All expenditure incurred in the running of the Loan Fund and in
maintaining the capital assets in a state of cfficiency have been charge to
revenue in arriving at the profit for the year.

All expenditure incurred in the acquisition, extension or improvement of
assets of a permanent nature in order to Carry on or increase the carning
capacity of the Loan Fund has been treated as capital expenditure.
